< review>
I called ahead to try making an appointment for both my, and their, convenience.

The guy that answered the phone sounded like he couldn't hang up fast enough. He was super monotone, just said "okay" a lot, and never asked for my name.

When I arrived there were three guys inside that worked there, and no customers. I was greeted nicely, and we got to it.

I went in to clean up my beard lines and make them more symmetrical. He did an alright job over all, but didn't really ask any questions about what I was going for specifically, which was kinda weird. On the other hand, I didn't offer up any commentary, so I don't fault him on it. When he shaved around the beard lines he didn't do a great job. I know because he came back in with a safety razor afterwards, which was weird. It was a cold shave with shaving cream applied with his fingers, so that might have played a role.  He cut my neck in a bunch of spots, but that does happen I suppose. I also noticed a lot of hair and a significant amount of shaving cream on my neck after I got to the car. While checking I was mostly concerned with the line shape and didn't notice. Not a huge deal, but little things add up to make an experience good or bad in my opinion.

I have a short list of places I usually go for a shave, but today I was in a hurry so I googled around for a decent place nearby. I'd say it's fine if you're crunched for time. If you can wait I'd suggest finding a place that specializes in a good shave.</review>

<text>Great takeaway gem in DTLA! Highly, highly recommend the porchetta, you get super juicy pork with perfect crispy skin, which contrasts perfectly with the picked cucumber and radish to cut the fattiness and leave the meal not feeling too heavy. Also, the upgrade to char siu fried rice is worth it for that little extra indulgence! Overall, the price is very reasonable for the spectacular food you get.

They have a special Saturday only roast duck but make sure to get it early because they literally always run out! You can also call ahead and reserve and order in the morning.

Finally, I recommend pairing their meal with a classic lemon tea.

I read about Rice Box in a recent article that discussed Hong Kong style BBQ.  RiceBox is located in the Spring Street Arcade which I've wanted to check out for a while too so we decided to go.  We visited on a Friday night.  RiceBox is pretty small, almost a food court situation, and they were continually busy, even at night when the Spring Street Arcade is fairly dead.  The person who was at the counter was super nice, friendly, and helpful!  The food was great.  BBQ Pork was awesome and the pork and cheese egg rolls were a new flavor experience for me. < text>
This is a review for their soft opening, so the quality of food here can change in the future. Food here are pretty simple, char-siu rice, bao, chicken rice, etc. But what should be simple and tasty dishes are not executed well - everything is over cooked and dry. Having lived in Hong Kong while growing up, I really miss traditional Cantonese cuisine. This spot is traditional Cantonese food elevated. No MSG, Organic, No Antibiotics... and the place is clean and well put-together, with lots of little details of Hong Kong sprinkled throughout the decorations.

The food is phenomenal. Definitely give their Cheese Bao a try. It's traditional steamed Cha Siu Bao mixed with melted cheese all inside a marbled-looking Bao... Difficult to explain but trust me, it's good!< /text>

<rate>3<//rate>< text>
I love HK BBQ and this place does it well, but I do not think it is worth the price. My bf and I did the build-your-own box with OG Char Siu and Porchetta with a fried egg and ordered the Salt and Pepper wings.

When the food came out the box was about the same size as those square Styrofoam takeout boxes and we got about 7 or 8 tiny wings. The wings were the tastiest thing out of everything that we got. I loved the seasoning on the wings and the birds eye chili provided some good heat to them. I ended up mixing whatever fell off the wings into the rice box because the rice box was bland.

Half of the box was rice and the other half was split between the meat and veggies. The Char Siu was good but not that amazing. It tasted mostly of hoisin sauce. I feel like I could have just bought a whole slab of char siu pork from Sam Woo for about the same taste and cheaper price. The Porchetta was much better than the Char Siu but we did end up with maybe 5 pieces so it wasn't that impressive.

Total we paid for these 2 items with tax and tip was about $30. I was pretty disappointed with this place since the photos of the food here looked so good. I guess photos can be deceiving. I don't think I'd come back any time soon.<//text>

<GmapID>0x80c2c74937227c39:0xa97e2044f8df0738< /GmapID>< Text>
Finally a place for good Cantonese BBQ that's just not in the SGV area! (And not full of MSG) I came upon this place through Eater's recommendation and I was very excited to try since it's hard to come by good Cantonese food in LA.

Parking is a pain but thank God there is a parking lot right next to the Spring Arcade and being downtown, $9 all day parking really isn't that bad since meter parking is pretty much the same during weekdays for 2 hours or so.

I loved the decor of the place, especially their neon red sign that says 'rice' and their logo, which is the famous Stephen Chow's butcher look from 'From Beijing With Love'. Super cool! Seating might be a bit tough since the place is very small but since I know it's suppose to be a to-go joint, it didn't bother me much.

Now, the food!!! I love, love, love, love their Porchetta! Crunchy on the outside, soft and juicy on the inside. Yum! Their char-siu was also spot-on, really reminded me of the char-siu that I used to get with my dad in Hong Kong when I was young. Best part is knowing that there are no artificial coloring involved made it that much better! Their vegan shrooming buns are also a must get! I'm not a big fan of mushrooms but that, 'oh my bun', it was delicious!! I can't wait to try  the black soy chicken!! Definitely coming back!< /Text>

He does a cursory "inspection" in the attic, failing to notice we actually have two separate attic spaces due to an addition. He spends 5 minutes walking the perimeter of the house, failing to notice the active infestation we have in the fascia. He never even bothered to go under the house to look for subterranean termites, which we know we have. So after the 20-minute "inspection",  I get the sales pitch which is basically the cost of the tenting and the special spray that causes termites to die when they land on the treated surface (Really?
